# *Star Wars*: Episode IV *A New Hope*

[View source](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_IV_A_New_Hope?action=edit) 

* [History](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_IV_A_New_Hope?action=history)

[[Source]](https://starwars.fandom.com/wiki/Template:Movie)

:   "*A film for a generation growing up without fairy tales.*"
:   ―George Lucas[[4]](#cite_note-Topps-4)

***Star Wars*: Episode IV *A New Hope***, originally released as ***Star Wars***, is a [1977](/wiki/1977 "1977") space opera film written and directed by [George Lucas](/wiki/George_Lucas "George Lucas"). It is the first part of the *[Star Wars](/wiki/Star_Wars "Star Wars")* [original trilogy](/wiki/Original_trilogy "Original trilogy") and the first *Star Wars* film released.

The film is set 19 [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") after the [formation](/wiki/Proclamation_of_the_New_Order "Proclamation of the New Order") of the [Galactic Empire](/wiki/Galactic_Empire "Galactic Empire") and the events of *[Revenge of the Sith](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_III_Revenge_of_the_Sith "Star Wars: Episode III Revenge of the Sith")*; construction has finished on the [Death Star](/wiki/DS-1_Orbital_Battle_Station "DS-1 Orbital Battle Station"), a weapon capable of destroying a [planet](/wiki/Planet "Planet"). After [Princess](/wiki/Princess "Princess") [Leia Organa](/wiki/Leia_Skywalker_Organa_Solo "Leia Skywalker Organa Solo"), a leader of the [Rebel Alliance](/wiki/Alliance_to_Restore_the_Republic "Alliance to Restore the Republic"), receives the weapon's plans in the hope of finding a weakness, she is kidnapped and taken to the Death Star. Meanwhile, a young [farmer](/wiki/Moisture_farmer "Moisture farmer") named [Luke Skywalker](/wiki/Luke_Skywalker "Luke Skywalker") meets [Obi-Wan Kenobi](/wiki/Obi-Wan_Kenobi "Obi-Wan Kenobi"), who has lived in seclusion for years on the desert planet of [Tatooine](/wiki/Tatooine "Tatooine"). When [Luke's home](/wiki/Lars_homestead "Lars homestead") is burned and his [aunt](/wiki/Beru_Whitesun_Lars "Beru Whitesun Lars") and [uncle](/wiki/Owen_Lars "Owen Lars") killed, Obi-Wan begins Luke's [Jedi](/wiki/Jedi "Jedi") [training](/wiki/Jedi_training "Jedi training") as they—along with [Han Solo](/wiki/Han_Solo "Han Solo"), [Chewbacca](/wiki/Chewbacca "Chewbacca"), [C-3PO](/wiki/C-3PO "C-3PO"), and [R2-D2](/wiki/R2-D2 "R2-D2") attempt to rescue the princess from the Empire.

Inspired by films like the *[Flash Gordon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flash_Gordon_(serial) "wikipedia:Flash Gordon (serial)")* [serials](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Movie_serial "wikipedia:Movie serial") and the [samurai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samurai "wikipedia:Samurai") films of [Akira Kurosawa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Akira_Kurosawa "wikipedia:Akira Kurosawa"), as well as such critical works as [Joseph Campbell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Campbell "wikipedia:Joseph Campbell")'s *[The Hero with a Thousand Faces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Hero_with_a_Thousand_Faces "wikipedia:The Hero with a Thousand Faces")* and [Frank Herbert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Herbert "wikipedia:Frank Herbert")'s *[Dune](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dune_(franchise) "wikipedia:Dune (franchise)")* books, Lucas began work on *Star Wars* in 1974. Ground-breaking in its use of [special effects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_effect "wikipedia:Special effect"), this is considered to be among the most successful—and most influential—films of all time. Produced with a budget of [US$](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/US$ "wikipedia:US$")11,000,000 and released on [May 25](/wiki/May_25 "May 25"), 1977, the film became one of the most successful of all time, earning $215 million in the [United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States "wikipedia:United States") and $337 million overseas during its original theatrical release, as well as winning several film awards, including 10 [Academy Award](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Award "wikipedia:Academy Award") nominations. It was re-released several times, sometimes with [significant changes](/wiki/List_of_changes_in_Star_Wars_re-releases "List of changes in Star Wars re-releases"); the most notable versions were the 1997 [Special Edition](/wiki/The_Star_Wars_Trilogy_Special_Edition "The Star Wars Trilogy Special Edition") and the 2004 [DVD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DVD "wikipedia:DVD"), which were modified with [CGI](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_generated_imagery "wikipedia:Computer generated imagery") effects and recreated scenes. It was re-released in the Blu-ray format in [September](/wiki/September "September") of [2011](/wiki/2011 "2011"). The film was selected to be preserved by the [Library of Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Library_of_Congress "wikipedia:Library of Congress") as part of its [National Film Registry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Film_Registry "wikipedia:National Film Registry"). The film was selected in 1989, the program's first year in existence.

## Opening crawl

| Episode IV A NEW HOPE |
| --- |
| ``` It is a period of civil war. Rebel spaceships, striking from a hidden base, have won their first victory against the evil Galactic Empire.  During the battle, Rebel spies managed to steal secret plans to the Empire's ultimate weapon, the DEATH STAR, an armored space station with enough power to destroy an entire planet.  Pursued by the Empire's sinister agents, Princess Leia races home aboard her starship, custodian of the stolen plans that can save her people and restore freedom to the galaxy.... ``` |
|  |

## Plot summary

### [Assault on *Tantive IV*](/wiki/Secret_mission_to_Tatooine "Secret mission to Tatooine")

Nineteen [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") after the [formation](/wiki/Proclamation_of_the_New_Order "Proclamation of the New Order") of the [Galactic Empire](/wiki/Galactic_Empire "Galactic Empire"), [the galaxy](/wiki/The_galaxy "The galaxy") is in a state of [civil war](/wiki/Galactic_Civil_War "Galactic Civil War"). The [Rebel Alliance](/wiki/Alliance_to_Restore_the_Republic "Alliance to Restore the Republic") has won their first major victory by [stealing](/wiki/Battle_of_Scarif "Battle of Scarif") [plans](/wiki/Death_Star_plans "Death Star plans") to the Galactic Empire's secret weapon, the [Death Star](/wiki/DS-1_Orbital_Battle_Station "DS-1 Orbital Battle Station"). Hoping that the stolen plans can save her [people](/wiki/Alderaanian "Alderaanian") and restore freedom to the galaxy, [Princess](/wiki/Princess "Princess") [Leia Organa](/wiki/Leia_Skywalker_Organa_Solo "Leia Skywalker Organa Solo"), who is in custody of the plans, attempts to race home aboard the *[Tantive IV](/wiki/Tantive_IV "Tantive IV")*. However, her ship is intercepted by the [*Imperial* *I*-class](/wiki/Imperial_I-class_Star_Destroyer "Imperial I-class Star Destroyer") [Star Destroyer](/wiki/Star_Destroyer "Star Destroyer") *[Devastator](/wiki/Devastator "Devastator")* over the [desert](/wiki/Desert "Desert") [planet](/wiki/Planet "Planet") of [Tatooine](/wiki/Tatooine "Tatooine").

 [![Princess Leia is kidnapped by the Galactic Empire.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/02/Devastatortantiveiv.png/revision/latest?cb=20201017104531) [![Princess Leia is kidnapped by the Galactic Empire.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/02/Devastatortantiveiv.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20201017104531)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/02/Devastatortantiveiv.png/revision/latest?cb=20201017104531) 

Princess Leia is kidnapped by the Galactic Empire.

 

The ship is captured, and several Imperial [stormtroopers](/wiki/Stormtrooper "Stormtrooper") come aboard. After defeating the small number of [guards](/wiki/Rebel_trooper "Rebel trooper") defending the ship, the [Sith Lord](/wiki/Sith_Lord "Sith Lord") [Darth Vader](/wiki/Anakin_Skywalker "Anakin Skywalker") arrives to assess the damage. Vader is outraged and questions [Captain Antilles](/wiki/Raymus_Antilles "Raymus Antilles"), whom he eventually strangles and kills. Hiding on the ship, Princess Leia is able to record a [holographic](/wiki/Hologram "Hologram") message with the help of [R2-D2](/wiki/R2-D2 "R2-D2"), and gives the [droid](/wiki/Droid "Droid") the plans for the Death Star and the responsibility of taking the message to [Obi-Wan Kenobi](/wiki/Obi-Wan_Kenobi "Obi-Wan Kenobi"), a Jedi-in-hiding on Tatooine. Leia is spotted by stormtroopers and they shoot her with a stun blast and bring her before Vader. Leia claims she and the ship's crew were on a diplomatic mission to [Alderaan](/wiki/Alderaan "Alderaan"), but is disbelieved by Vader, who denounces her as a traitor and has her taken prisoner. Vader orders a message be sent to the [Imperial Senate](/wiki/Imperial_Senate "Imperial Senate"), informing them that the ship was destroyed, with everyone on board killed. R2-D2 and [C-3PO](/wiki/C-3PO "C-3PO") use an escape pod in order to escape the ship and reach the planet of Tatooine below, narrowly escaping destruction by an Imperial cannon when the operators do not detect the droids in the pod.

### Luke's destiny

 [![Luke Skywalker receives his father's lightsaber.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/92/Lukesaberanh.png/revision/latest?cb=20130228054320) [![Luke Skywalker receives his father's lightsaber.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/92/Lukesaberanh.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20130228054320)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/92/Lukesaberanh.png/revision/latest?cb=20130228054320) 

Luke Skywalker receives his father's lightsaber.

 

:   "*There's nothing for me here now. I want to learn the ways of the Force and become a Jedi like my father.*"
:   ―Luke Skywalker[[1]](#cite_note-Episode-1)

After arguing and going their separate ways for a while, the droids are individually picked up by [Jawa](/wiki/Jawa "Jawa") traders and brought aboard a [sandcrawler](/wiki/Sandcrawler "Sandcrawler"). They are later bought by moisture farmer [Owen Lars](/wiki/Owen_Lars "Owen Lars") and his nephew, [Luke Skywalker](/wiki/Luke_Skywalker "Luke Skywalker"), a young farmer who lost his parents as a baby and hopes to one day be a starfighter pilot just like his friends. While cleaning R2, Luke discovers a short portion of the hologram. At the mention of Obi Wan, he wonders if she means his neighbor Ben Kenobi.

While eating dinner with Owen and his Aunt [Beru Whitesun Lars](/wiki/Beru_Whitesun_Lars "Beru Whitesun Lars"), Owen asks Luke to take R2 to [Anchorhead](/wiki/Anchorhead "Anchorhead") the next day to have his memory wiped, and expresses his hope Luke will stay with them for one more harvest season before applying to the [Academy](/wiki/Imperial_Academy "Imperial Academy"). R2 escapes from the Lars' homestead in search of Obi-Wan, whom the droid claims to be the property of. Luke and C-3PO search the desert and find R2 the next day, only to be attacked by [sand people](/wiki/Tusken_Raider "Tusken Raider"). Luke and his droids are rescued by Ben Kenobi, who confirms he is Obi-Wan.

At his home, Obi-Wan gives Luke his father's [lightsaber](/wiki/Lightsaber "Lightsaber"), as Obi-Wan recalls his own friendship with Luke's father. He tells Luke that he and his father were a part of the [Jedi](/wiki/Jedi "Jedi") order that once protected the galaxy before the Empire took over and that Darth Vader was once his apprentice before he fell to the [dark side of the Force](/wiki/Dark_side_of_the_Force "Dark side of the Force") and murdered Luke's father. After viewing Princess Leia's full recording, Obi-Wan attempts to persuade Luke to accompany him to Alderaan. Luke refuses but agrees to take Obi-Wan as far as Anchorhead. On the way, the group discovers the remains of the sandcrawler, the Jawas having been killed by stormtroopers searching for the droids. With dawning horror, Luke hurries home only to find it burning and his aunt and uncle's charred remains, both brutally murdered by the same stormtroopers.

Luke returns upset, but Obi-Wan tells him there was nothing he could do, and that he would have been killed too and the plans would be in possession of the Empire. With nothing keeping him on Tatooine, Luke, Obi Wan, and the two droids travel to [Mos Eisley](/wiki/Mos_Eisley "Mos Eisley") to find passage to Alderaan, Princess Leia's home planet.

Aboard the Death Star, [Cassio Tagge](/wiki/Cassio_Tagge "Cassio Tagge") argues with [Conan Antonio Motti](/wiki/Conan_Antonio_Motti "Conan Antonio Motti") about the stations vulnerability to the rebels and points out that the rebellion has been gaining support within the imperial senate. [Wilhuff Tarkin](/wiki/Wilhuff_Tarkin "Wilhuff Tarkin") enters the room with Darth Vader and informs them that the [Emperor](/wiki/Emperor "Emperor") has dissolved the senate completely, sweeping away the last remnant of the Old Republic. Believing fear will keep the galaxy in line, Motti boasts the power of the Death Star, to which Vader replies that its power is insignificant compared to [the Force](/wiki/The_Force "The Force"). When Motti mocks Vader's belief in the Force, Vader [Force chokes](/wiki/Force_choke "Force choke") him until Tarkin orders him to stop, and expresses his own desire to crush the Rebellion.

Back in Mos Eisley, Luke, Obi-Wan and the droids run into a patrol of stormtroopers, who ask for their identification. Obi-Wan uses a [Jedi mind trick](/wiki/Mind_trick "Mind trick") on the lead trooper, who lets them pass. Arriving at [Chalmun's Spaceport Cantina](/wiki/Chalmun%27s_Spaceport_Cantina "Chalmun's Spaceport Cantina"), the group hires [smuggler](/wiki/Smuggler "Smuggler") [Han Solo](/wiki/Han_Solo "Han Solo") and his [First Mate](/wiki/First_Mate "First Mate"), a [Wookiee](/wiki/Wookiee "Wookiee") named [Chewbacca](/wiki/Chewbacca "Chewbacca"), for 17,000 [credits](/wiki/Galactic_Credit_Standard "Galactic Credit Standard"), 2,000 in advance and 15,000 upon arrival, to take the four of them to Alderaan aboard their ship, the *[Millennium Falcon](/wiki/Millennium_Falcon "Millennium Falcon")*. Han has a brief run-in with [Greedo](/wiki/Greedo "Greedo") over his debts to crime lord [Jabba the Hutt](/wiki/Jabba_Desilijic_Tiure "Jabba Desilijic Tiure"), which ends with Han fatally [shooting](/wiki/Han_shot_first "Han shot first") Greedo. Jabba later confronts Han in the *Falcon*'s docking bay, scolding him for killing Greedo. Han defends the actions that offended Jabba (dumping a load of cargo when confronted by an Imperial patrol) and promises he'll pay the gangster what he owes. Luke, Ben and the droids arrive at the *Falcon*'s hangar. A brief scuffle with stormtroopers ensues, and the *Falcon* escapes Imperial Star Destroyers over Tatooine and sets a course to Alderaan, unaware that the Death Star has just arrived there as well.

### Rescue of the princess

:   "*Here's where the fun begins!*"
:   ―Han Solo[[1]](#cite_note-Episode-1)

Leia, having resisted being tortured with a [mind probe](/wiki/Mind_probe "Mind probe") for the location of the Rebel Alliance's headquarters, is brought before [Grand Moff](/wiki/Grand_Moff "Grand Moff") [Tarkin](/wiki/Wilhuff_Tarkin "Wilhuff Tarkin"). Tarkin threatens to use the Death Star's [superlaser](/wiki/Superlaser "Superlaser") on Leia's [homeworld](/wiki/Homeworld "Homeworld") of Alderaan if she does not tell them the Rebel base's location. She reluctantly tells them the base is on [Dantooine](/wiki/Dantooine "Dantooine"), but Tarkin orders Alderaan to be destroyed anyway for its role in supporting the rebels.

Aboard the Millennium Falcon, Obi-Wan feels a [great disturbance in the Force](/wiki/Disturbance_in_the_Force "Disturbance in the Force") while Luke undergoes Lightsaber training with a [training remote](/wiki/Marksman-H_training_remote "Marksman-H training remote"). Upon dropping out of [hyperspace](/wiki/Hyperspace "Hyperspace"), they find what seems to be an [asteroid field](/wiki/Alderaanian_Graveyard "Alderaanian Graveyard") in Alderaan's place. The *Millennium Falcon* is then pulled aboard the Death Star by its powerful [tractor beam](/wiki/Tractor_beam "Tractor beam").

 [![Heroes en route to the Death Star](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/14/Got_A_Bad_feeling.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20070922141109) [![Heroes en route to the Death Star](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/14/Got_A_Bad_feeling.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20070922141109)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/14/Got_A_Bad_feeling.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20070922141109) 

Heroes en route to the Death Star

 

Tarkin and Vader discover that Leia lied about the Rebel base's location when their forces only discover the ruins of a base on Dantooine. Tarkin orders her to be executed.

Having docked with the Death Star, Solo and the others ambush two stormtroopers and the Imperial scanning crew sent to investigate the Falcon by hiding in hidden smuggling compartments. With Han and Luke now disguised as the two stormtroopers, the group storms a control room to figure out how to escape. Obi-Wan separates from the group to disable the tractor beam, leaving the others alone. While connected to the Imperial Network, R2-D2 discovers Princess Leia is aboard the station and is set for termination. Luke convinces Han and Chewbacca to [rescue her](/wiki/Rescue_of_Princess_Leia "Rescue of Princess Leia") with the vague promise of a grand reward. Han and Chewbacca reluctantly agree. Luke plans to march into [Detention Block AA-23](/wiki/Detention_Block_AA-23 "Detention Block AA-23"), claiming that Chewbacca is part of a prisoner transfer. C-3PO and R2-D2 are instructed to remain behind, and the trio sets off on their rescue attempt. Upon being met with suspicion, they are quick to subdue the officers and guards in the princess's cell block. Luke frees Leia from her cell, but the group are pinned down by a squad of stormtroopers. Leia takes charge, blasting a hole in a nearby grate and jumping through while Chewbacca, Luke, and Han all dive after the princess.

The chute ends up leading to a [garbage compactor](/wiki/Garbage_compactor "Garbage compactor") that is also home to a [resident](/wiki/Omi "Omi") [dianoga](/wiki/Dianoga "Dianoga"). Soon after landing, the creature pulls Luke under the surface, but releases him and is scared away when the Imperials realize where the heroes escaped to and activate the compactor. As the walls close in on the foursome, Luke desperately calls to C-3PO over his comlink asking for the compactor to be shut down. Leia struggles to get to the top and Chewbacca tries to unlock the door. R2-D2 manages to shut down the compactor just in time, although, amidst the muffled cries of joy over the comlink, C-3PO is briefly convinced that his master and friends have been crushed.

After escaping from the trash compactor, the group hurries back to the *Millennium Falcon*, hoping that Obi-Wan has successfully shut down the tractor beam. Leia and Han bicker about who is in charge of the mission, while Han muses no reward is worth dealing with Leia's scathing criticism. Luke and Leia briefly become separated from Han and Chewie when Han chases after a group of stormtroopers, only to run into a whole battalion and be chased by them instead. Luke and Leia nearly run into a large chasm and are forced to swing across with a [grappling hook](/wiki/Grappling_hook "Grappling hook") amongst blaster fire, with Leia giving Luke a brief kiss "for luck". The group soon reunite and make their way back to the *Falcon*.

### Sacrifice and victory

 [!["You can't win, Darth. If you strike me down, I shall become more powerful than you can possibly imagine](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5c/Obiwanvaderanhduel.png/revision/latest?cb=20130314001347) [!["You can't win, Darth. If you strike me down, I shall become more powerful than you can possibly imagine](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5c/Obiwanvaderanhduel.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20130314001347)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5c/Obiwanvaderanhduel.png/revision/latest?cb=20130314001347) 

"You can't win, Darth. If you strike me down, I shall become more powerful than you can possibly imagine."

 

:   "*This will be a day long remembered. It has seen the end of Kenobi. It will soon see the end of the Rebellion.*"
:   ―Darth Vader[[1]](#cite_note-Episode-1)

Meanwhile, Obi-Wan, remaining completely undetected, shuts down the tractor beam. Vader, however, had sensed his presence through the Force, and, while Obi-Wan makes his way to the *Millennium Falcon*, confronts his old master and engages him in a lightsaber duel. Luke and the others make it back to the Falcon, where Luke and several stormtroopers witness the battle. Sparing one last glance at Luke, Obi-Wan allows himself to be struck down by Vader, thus becoming one with the Force and allowing Luke and the others to escape. Horrified and angered at having witnessed Obi-Wan's demise at the hands of Vader, Luke and the others are forced to flee on the *Millennium Falcon* under a hail of blaster fire from the stormtroopers.

Still mourning Obi-Wan's death, Luke helps Solo fend off a squadron of [TIE fighters](/wiki/TIE/ln_space_superiority_starfighter "TIE/ln space superiority starfighter"). Despite their supposed victory, Leia correctly believes the Empire let them go in order to track them to the rebel base. The crew of the *Falcon* finally meets the Rebel Alliance on the moon of [Yavin 4](/wiki/Yavin_4 "Yavin 4"), and the information in R2-D2 is turned over to them. [General](/wiki/General "General") [Dodonna](/wiki/Jan_Dodonna "Jan Dodonna") plans the attack on the Death Star, as the plans reveal a weakness in the Death Stars design in the form of a thermal exhaust port leading to the station's reactor. Believing a direct hit with [proton torpedos](/wiki/Proton_torpedo "Proton torpedo") will cause a chain reaction that will destroy the station, Dodanna orders the pilots to man their ships in preparation for the battle. To Luke's dismay, Han leaves after receiving his reward to settle his debts.

 [![Rebel fighters approach the Death Star.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/b/bd/Battle_of_Yavin.png/revision/latest?cb=20220716182807) [![Rebel fighters approach the Death Star.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/b/bd/Battle_of_Yavin.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20220716182807)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/b/bd/Battle_of_Yavin.png/revision/latest?cb=20220716182807) 

Rebel fighters approach the Death Star.

 

The Rebel strike force begins its attack on the Death Star, as the battle station approaches Yavin 4. A group of [X-wing](/wiki/X-wing_starfighter "X-wing starfighter"), and [Y-wing starfighters](/wiki/BTL_Y-wing_starfighter "BTL Y-wing starfighter"), Luke among them, assault a trench on the Death Star's surface to hit the station's vulnerable spot before it can destroy the Alliance's base. During this, most of the Rebel craft, including Luke's friend [Biggs Darklighter](/wiki/Biggs_Darklighter "Biggs Darklighter"), are picked off by a group of Imperial fighters led by Darth Vader. Tarkin is told by an Imperial officer that the Rebels do pose a danger, but Tarkin refuses to evacuate in their supposed moment of triumph. With the Death Star only minutes from being in range to destroy Yavin 4, Luke makes one last run down the trench toward the exhaust port. Just as Vader opens fire on Luke from his personal [TIE Advanced x1](/wiki/TIE_Advanced_x1 "TIE Advanced x1"), Han returns in the *Millennium Falcon* and attacks the Imperials, resulting in Vader's TIE getting knocked out of the trench. Luke, aided by the voice of Kenobi and guided by the Force, accurately fires two proton torpedoes into the exhaust port and retreats. Moments later the battle station explodes, killing Tarkin and everyone on board, while Vader escapes into space.

The few remaining ships (those of [Wedge Antilles](/wiki/Wedge_Antilles "Wedge Antilles"), Luke, Han, and a [Y-wing Pilot](/wiki/Evaan_Verlaine "Evaan Verlaine")) return to Yavin 4 and a [victory ceremony](/wiki/Royal_Award_Ceremony "Royal Award Ceremony") commences, where [medals](/wiki/Medal_of_Bravery "Medal of Bravery") are presented to the heroes, Han Solo and Luke Skywalker, by Princess Leia, as the rebels give them a standing ovation.

## Development

### Conception

During post-production on his previous film, *[American Graffiti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Graffiti "wikipedia:American Graffiti")*, Lucas repeatedly discussed the concept of a "[space opera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_opera "wikipedia:Space opera")" with producer [Gary Kurtz](/wiki/Gary_Kurtz "Gary Kurtz"). In January 1973 Lucas began work on this, and by May had prepared a [14-page story outline](/wiki/The_Star_Wars_story_synopsis "The Star Wars story synopsis") for distribution among film studios.[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5) He had originally envisioned the film as being a continuation of both *American Graffiti* and '['Apocalypse Now](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apocalypse_Now "wikipedia:Apocalypse Now") *(the latter of which he helped make before [Warner Bros. Studios](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warner_Bros._Studios "wikipedia:Warner Bros. Studios") shut down his studio of [American Zoetrope](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Zoetrope "wikipedia:American Zoetrope") and thus forced him to hand over development to his compatriot, Francis Ford Coppola). His note for the basic plotline for the film, which was intended to be a response to the Vietnam War era, was that it involved "a [technological empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_of_America "wikipedia:United States of America") going after a [small band of freedom fighters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viet_Cong "wikipedia:Viet Cong")."[[6]](#cite_note-New_York_Post-6)[[7]](#cite_note-How_Star_Wars_Conquered_the_Universe-7) According to Walter Murch, a former associate of Lucas when the latter was filming* Apocalypse Now*, the space opera setting was conceived in large part because, due to the Vietnam War still going on, the audiences would not have been receptive to a direct attack on American involvement in Vietnam.[[8]](#cite_note-Metaphor-8)[[9]](#cite_note-Walter_Murch-9) Because of its [outer space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outer_space "wikipedia:Outer space") setting, the story was viewed as science fiction, an unpopular genre at the box office. Lucas later proposed that terms like "space fantasy" or "science fantasy" better fit the story.[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5) He brought the outline to [Universal Studios](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Studios "wikipedia:Universal Studios") and [United Artists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Artists "wikipedia:United Artists"); both rejected the project (the former refused directly, while the latter withheld their answer until after the 10 day wait period ended).[[6]](#cite_note-New_York_Post-6)[[10]](#cite_note-KurtzIGN1-10)[[7]](#cite_note-How_Star_Wars_Conquered_the_Universe-7) He also turned to [Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures](/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Motion_Pictures "Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures"), though they also turned him down.[[6]](#cite_note-New_York_Post-6)[[7]](#cite_note-How_Star_Wars_Conquered_the_Universe-7) Lucas disliked the studio system because his previous two films,* American Graffiti *and* [THX 1138](/wiki/1138_(easter_egg) "1138 (easter egg)")*, had been re-edited without his consent.[[11]](#cite_note-Wired-11) Still, aware that studios were unavoidable, he pursued [Alan Ladd, Jr.](/wiki/Alan_Ladd,_Jr. "Alan Ladd, Jr."), the head of [20th Century Fox](/wiki/20th_Century_Studios "20th Century Studios"). Although Ladd did not grasp the technical side of the project, he believed that Lucas was talented. Lucas later stated that Ladd "invested in me, [but] he did not invest in the movie."[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5)*

### Production

Lucas wrote multiple drafts of the script: a [rough draft](/wiki/The_Star_Wars_rough_draft "The Star Wars rough draft") in May and a [first draft](/wiki/The_Star_Wars_first_draft "The Star Wars first draft") in July 1974, a second draft titled, *[Adventures of the Starkiller as taken from the Journal of the Whills, Saga I: The Star Wars](/wiki/Adventures_of_the_Starkiller,_Episode_I:_The_Star_Wars "Adventures of the Starkiller, Episode I: The Star Wars")* in January and a third titled, *[The Star Wars: From The Adventures of Luke Starkiller](/wiki/The_Star_Wars:_From_The_Adventures_of_Luke_Starkiller "The Star Wars: From The Adventures of Luke Starkiller")* in August 1975.

As the draft developed, the characters evolved significantly. Early in development, Luke Skywalker's character changed from a 60-year-old general to a member of a family of [dwarfs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dwarf "wikipedia:Dwarf");[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5)[[12]](#cite_note-Characters-12) the [Corellian](/wiki/Corellia "Corellia") smuggler, [Han Solo](/wiki/Han_Solo "Han Solo"), was envisioned as a large, green-skinned monster with gills.[[12]](#cite_note-Characters-12) [Chewbacca](/wiki/Chewbacca "Chewbacca") was inspired by Lucas' Alaskan malamute dog, Indiana, who often acted as the director's "co-pilot" by sitting in the passenger seat of his car.[[12]](#cite_note-Characters-12) The Force, a mysterious energy field, was initially conceived as the [Kyber crystal](/wiki/Kyber_crystal "Kyber crystal"), a "galactic holy grail."[[13]](#cite_note-Genesis-13)[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5) The completed script was too long for one movie; however, Lucas refused to condense it. Instead, he expanded the first third of it into one movie and left the rest for two future films, effectively creating the [original *Star Wars* trilogy](/wiki/Original_trilogy "Original trilogy").[[14]](#cite_note-Maker-14)[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5)[[15]](#cite_note-:5-15)

Lucas hired conceptual artist [Ralph McQuarrie](/wiki/Ralph_McQuarrie "Ralph McQuarrie") to create paintings of certain scenes during screenwriting. When Lucas delivered his screenplay to the studio, he included several of McQuarrie's paintings.[[16]](#cite_note-McQuarrie-16) 20th Century Fox approved a budget of $8,250,000; *American Graffiti*'s positive reviews allowed Lucas to renegotiate his deal with Alan Ladd, Jr. and request the sequel rights to the film. For Lucas, this deal protected *Star Wars*' unwritten segments and most of the merchandising profits.[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5)[[17]](#cite_note-17)

 [![A  panel depicting   searching for  and ](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/01/Dewback_sketch.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20070721043741) [![A  panel depicting   searching for  and ](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/01/Dewback_sketch.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/220?cb=20070721043741)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/01/Dewback_sketch.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20070721043741) 

A [storyboard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/storyboard "wikipedia:storyboard") panel depicting [Imperial](/wiki/Galactic_Empire "Galactic Empire") [stormtroopers](/wiki/Stormtrooper "Stormtrooper") searching for [R2-D2](/wiki/R2-D2 "R2-D2") and [C-3PO](/wiki/C-3PO "C-3PO")

 

In 1975, Lucas founded the visual effects company [Industrial Light & Magic](/wiki/Industrial_Light_%26_Magic "Industrial Light & Magic") (ILM) after discovering that 20th Century Fox's visual effects department had been disbanded. ILM began its work on *Star Wars* in a warehouse in [Van Nuys, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Van_Nuys,_California "wikipedia:Van Nuys, California"). Lucas himself bought old equipment for pennies on the dollar.[[18]](#cite_note-encore-18) traditionally, models were filmed by moving them in front of a stationary camera.[[19]](#cite_note-garden-19) Most of the visual effects used [motion control photography](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Motion_control_photography "wikipedia:Motion control photography"), which creates the illusion of size by employing small models and slowly moving cameras called the [Dykstraflex](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dykstraflex "wikipedia:Dykstraflex").[[18]](#cite_note-encore-18) all the models would be shot in front of a blue screen, which would allow the placement of other elements into the scene, this process is called optical compositing.[[18]](#cite_note-encore-18) the team the special effects team retooled an optical printer that allowed separate film strips to be photographed and combined onto a single layer of film.[[18]](#cite_note-encore-18) artists created matt paintings to increase the scope and production value of a scene, by extending environments painted on glass, that would be photographed and combined with live-action elements.[[18]](#cite_note-encore-18) Model spaceships were constructed on the basis of drawings by [Joe Johnston](/wiki/Joe_Johnston "Joe Johnston"), input from Lucas, and paintings by McQuarrie. Lucas opted to abandon the traditional sleekness of science fiction by creating a "used universe" in which all devices, ships, and buildings looked aged and dirty.[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5)[[20]](#cite_note-Legacy-20)[[21]](#cite_note-ILM_Bio-21)

Filming began on [March 22](/wiki/March_22 "March 22"), [1976](/wiki/1976 "1976") in the [Tunisia](/wiki/Tunisia "Tunisia").[[22]](#cite_note-Episode_100-22) Lucas fell behind schedule in the first week of shooting due to a rare Tunisian rainstorm, malfunctioning props, and electronic breakdowns.[[23]](#cite_note-Heritage-23) When actor [Anthony Daniels](/wiki/Anthony_Daniels "Anthony Daniels") wore the C-3PO outfit for the first time, the left leg piece shattered down through the plastic covering his left foot, stabbing him. After completing filming in Tunisia, production moved into the more controlled environment of [Elstree Studios](/wiki/Elstree_Studios "Elstree Studios"), near London.[[23]](#cite_note-Heritage-23) However, significant problems, such as a [crew](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Film_crew "wikipedia:Film crew") that had little interest in the film, still arose.[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5)[[23]](#cite_note-Heritage-23) Most of the crew considered the project a "children's film," rarely took their work seriously, and often found it unintentionally humorous.[[24]](#cite_note-Star_Wars:_The_Legacy_Revealed-24) Actor [Kenny Baker](/wiki/Kenny_Baker "Kenny Baker") later confessed that he thought the film would be a failure.[[25]](#cite_note-Time77p57-25) [Harrison Ford](/wiki/Harrison_Ford "Harrison Ford") found the dialogue difficult, saying, "You can type this shit, George, but you sure can't say it."[[26]](#cite_note-Skywalking:_The_Life_and_Films_of_George_Lucas-26)

Lucas clashed with [director of photography](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Director_of_Photography "wikipedia:Director of Photography") [Gilbert Taylor](/wiki/Gilbert_Taylor "Gilbert Taylor"), whom producer Gary Kurtz called "old-school" and "crotchety."[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5)[[27]](#cite_note-Taylor3-27) Moreover, with a background in independent filmmaking, Lucas was accustomed to creating most of the elements of the film himself. His camera suggestions were rejected by an offended Taylor, who felt that Lucas was over-stepping his boundaries by giving specific instructions. Lucas eventually became frustrated that the costumes, sets and other elements were not living up to his original vision of *Star Wars*. He rarely spoke to the actors, who felt that he expected too much of them while providing little direction. His directions to the actors usually consisted of the words "faster" and "more intense."[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5)

Ladd offered Lucas some of the only support from the studio; he dealt with scrutiny from [board](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Board_of_directors "wikipedia:Board of directors") members over the rising budget and complex screenplay drafts. After production fell two weeks behind schedule, Ladd told Lucas that he had to finish production within a week or he would be forced to shut down production. The crew split into three units, led by Lucas, Kurtz, and production supervisor [Robert Watts](/wiki/Robert_Watts "Robert Watts"), respectively. Under the new system, the project met the studio's deadline.[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5)[[23]](#cite_note-Heritage-23) ILM concluded shooting on [April 22](/wiki/April_22 "April 22"), 1977 with shot 110P, that of a Star Destroyer.[[28]](#cite_note-swi95-28)

*Star Wars* was originally slated for release in [Christmas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christmas "wikipedia:Christmas") 1976; however, delays pushed the film's release to summer 1977. Already anxious about meeting his deadline, Lucas was shocked when his editor's first cut of the film was a "complete disaster." After attempting to persuade the original editor to cut the film his way, Lucas replaced the editor with [Paul Hirsch](/wiki/Paul_Hirsch "Paul Hirsch") and [Richard Chew](/wiki/Richard_Chew "Richard Chew"). He also allowed his then-wife [Marcia Lucas](/wiki/Marcia_Lucas "Marcia Lucas") to aid the editing process while she was cutting the film *[New York, New York](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York,_New_York_(film) "wikipedia:New York, New York (film)")* with Lucas' friend [Martin Scorsese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martin_Scorsese "wikipedia:Martin Scorsese"). Richard Chew found the film had an non-energetic pace; it had been cut in a by-the-book manner: scenes were played out in [master shots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Master_shot "wikipedia:Master shot") that flowed into [close-up](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Close-up "wikipedia:Close-up") coverage. He found that the pace was dictated by the actors instead of the cuts. Hirsch and Chew worked on two reels simultaneously; whoever finished first moved on to the next.[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5)

During production, the cast attempted to make Lucas laugh or smile as he often appeared depressed. At one point, the project became so demanding that Lucas was diagnosed with hypertension and exhaustion and was warned to reduce his stress level.[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5)[[23]](#cite_note-Heritage-23) [Post-production](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post-production "wikipedia:Post-production") was equally stressful due to increasing pressure from 20th Century Fox. Moreover, [Mark Hamill](/wiki/Mark_Hamill "Mark Hamill")'s face was injured in a car accident, which made reshoots impossible.[[23]](#cite_note-Heritage-23)

Meanwhile, ILM was struggling to achieve unprecedented special effects. The company had spent half of its budget on four shots that Lucas deemed unacceptable.[[23]](#cite_note-Heritage-23) Moreover, theories surfaced that the workers at ILM lacked discipline, forcing Lucas to intervene frequently to ensure that they were on schedule.[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5) With hundreds of uncompleted shots remaining, ILM was forced to finish a year's work in six months. Lucas inspired ILM by editing together aerial [dogfights](/wiki/Starfighter_combat "Starfighter combat") from old war films, which enhanced the pacing of the scenes.[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5)[[19]](#cite_note-garden-19)

During the chaos of production and post-production, the team made decisions about character voicing and [sound effects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sound_effect "wikipedia:Sound effect"). Sound designer [Ben Burtt](/wiki/Ben_Burtt "Ben Burtt") had created a library of sounds that Lucas referred to as an "organic soundtrack." For Chewbacca's growls, Burtt recorded and combined sounds made by dogs, bears, lions, tigers, and walruses to create phrases and sentences. Burtt created the robotic voice of R2-D2 by filtering his voice through an electronic synthesizer. Darth Vader's breathing was achieved by Burtt breathing through the mask of a [scuba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_set "wikipedia:Scuba set") tank implanted with a microphone.[[29]](#cite_note-Silicon-29) Lucas never intended to use the voice of [David Prowse](/wiki/David_Prowse "David Prowse"), who portrayed Darth Vader in costume, because of Prowse's thick English [West Country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Country "wikipedia:West Country") accent. He originally wanted [Orson Welles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orson_Welles "wikipedia:Orson Welles") to speak for Darth Vader. However, he felt that Welles' voice would be too recognizable, so he cast the lesser-known [James Earl Jones](/wiki/James_Earl_Jones "James Earl Jones").[[30]](#cite_note-30) Nor did Lucas intend to use Anthony Daniels' voice for C-3PO. Thirty well-established voice actors, such as [Stan Freberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stan_Freberg "wikipedia:Stan Freberg"), read for the voice of the droid. According to Daniels, one of the major voice actors recommended Daniels' voice for the role.[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5)[[12]](#cite_note-Characters-12)

The "Lost Cut" of *Star Wars* was edited by [John Jympson](/wiki/John_Jympson "John Jympson").[[31]](#cite_note-Insider_41-31) When Lucas screened an early cut of the film for his friends, among them directors [Brian De Palma](/wiki/Brian_De_Palma "Brian De Palma"), [John Milius](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Milius "wikipedia:John Milius") and [Steven Spielberg](/wiki/Steven_Spielberg "Steven Spielberg"), their reactions were disappointing. Spielberg, who claimed to have been the only person in the audience to have enjoyed the film,[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5) believed that the lack of enthusiasm was due to the absence of finished special effects. Lucas later said that the group was honest and seemed bemused by the film. In contrast, Alan Ladd, Jr. and the rest of 20th Century Fox loved the film; one of the executives, Gareth Wigan, told Lucas, "This is the greatest film I've ever seen," and cried during the screening. Lucas found the experience shocking and rewarding, having never gained any approval from studio executives before.[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5) Although the delays increased the budget from $8 million to $11 million, the film was still the least expensive of the *Star Wars* saga.

### Music

From the very beginning, Lucas' intention for "Star Wars" was that it would have very familiar sounding music, that despite the extraordinary visuals and events occurring onscreen, the music would be reminiscent of Earth and of the past. To that end, he originally wanted to fill the film with tracked classical music from various composers, in a similar fashion to *[2001: A Space Odyssey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2001:_A_Space_Odyssey "wikipedia:2001: A Space Odyssey")*.[[32]](#cite_note-FSM_1.97_MM_article-32) Lucas' friend, [Steven Spielberg](/wiki/Steven_Spielberg "Steven Spielberg"), recommended composer [John Williams](/wiki/John_Williams "John Williams") to Lucas after their recent collaboration on *[Jaws](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaws_(film) "wikipedia:Jaws (film)")* (1975). Spielberg convinced Lucas that he should meet with the composer, who in turn convinced him of the need for original music.[[33]](#cite_note-new_yorker_john_williams_interview-33) They also decided in this early meeting that the score should have a romantic musical sound, with leitmotifs for different characters and events, similar to the operas of [Richard Wagner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Wagner "wikipedia:Richard Wagner").[[34]](#cite_note-1997_liner_notes-34)

Rough cuts of "Star Wars" used something called a "temp score", referring to musical material that was there to find a rhythm while editing but would not be kept in the final cut as it would be replaced by the final score. These temp tracks would help to inspire the direction John Williams was to take with his score as he began writing it.[[35]](#cite_note-1977_liner_notes-35) Most of the temp tracks are not public knowledge, but some information has been revealed over the years. In one interview, editor [Paul Hirsch](/wiki/Paul_Hirsch "Paul Hirsch") confirmed that a cue from [Bernard Herrmann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bernard_Herrmann "wikipedia:Bernard Herrmann")'s *[Psycho](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psycho_(1960_film) "wikipedia:Psycho (1960 film)")* score containing the famous "3-note motif" was used to temp the scene where the heroes exit the smuggling chambers of the Millennium Falcon.[[36]](#cite_note-The_Making_of_Psycho-36) In another interview, Hirsch revealed that the opening to "The Sacrifice" from [Igor Stravinsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Igor_Stravinsky "wikipedia:Igor Stravinsky")'s "[The Rite of Spring](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Rite_of_Spring "wikipedia:The Rite of Spring")" was used to temp the scene in the desert, the Jawa scenes were temped from other parts of the same piece, and the Main Title crawl was temped with the overture of *[Ivanhoe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ivanhoe_(1952_film) "wikipedia:Ivanhoe (1952 film)")* by [Miklós Rózsa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mikl%C3%B3s_R%C3%B3zsa "wikipedia:Miklós Rózsa").[[37]](#cite_note-The_Making_of_Star_Wars_book-37) Later, in his own book, Hirsch would claim that the Main Title crawl was temped with [Erich Korngold](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erich_Korngold "wikipedia:Erich Korngold")'s theme to 1938's [The Adventures of Robin Hood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Adventures_of_Robin_Hood "wikipedia:The Adventures of Robin Hood"). It is unknown which of these claims is correct. Also in his book, Hirsch mentions that the Cantina scene was tracked by Benny Goodman's "Avalon" from his Carnegie Hall performance, some of the early battle footage was tracked with "Dance of the Adolescents" from "The Rite of Spring", and the approach to the Death Star was temped with the music from the approach to Kong Island from Max Steiner's King Kong score.[[38]](#cite_note-Paul_Hirsch_book-38) In an interview, sound editor Ben Burtt said that Antonín Dvořák's New World Symphony was temped into the medal ceremony (Hirsch mentioned this in his book too), and parts of Anton Bruckner's Ninth Symphony were temped as Luke's theme.[[37]](#cite_note-The_Making_of_Star_Wars_book-37) Homages to many of these known temp tracks appear in the final score. For example, the cue [1m5-2m1] Desert Song from *Star Wars* is extremely similar to the opening of the Stravinsky piece it was temped with. Further, the music in [1m2] Main Title that plays when the underbelly of the Star Destroyer flies over the camera is very similar to the ending of "Mars - The Bringer of War" from [Holst](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gustav_Holst "wikipedia:Gustav Holst")'s "[The Planets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Planets "wikipedia:The Planets")". Even the 3-note motif from *Psycho* appears in the very opening of the Star Wars cue [7m1-7m2 New] The Hatch Opens, exactly where the temp track would have been.

On January 10, 1977, Williams was invited to the spotting sessions, where he watched a rough cut of the film with Lucas, music supervisor [Lionel Newman](/wiki/Lionel_Newman "Lionel Newman"), music editor [Ken Wannberg](/wiki/Ken_Wannberg "Ken Wannberg"), producer [Gary Kurtz](/wiki/Gary_Kurtz "Gary Kurtz"), and film editor Paul Hirsch.[[37]](#cite_note-The_Making_of_Star_Wars_book-37)[[38]](#cite_note-Paul_Hirsch_book-38)[[39]](#cite_note-Paul_Duncan_tweet-39) Over the next several weeks, he would get to work writing the score. The way Williams wrote his score, he began by creating all the various leitmotifs and character themes (such as "[Luke's Theme](/wiki/Star_Wars_Main_Title "Star Wars Main Title")," "[Leia's theme](/wiki/Princess_Leia%27s_Theme "Princess Leia's Theme")," and "[Ben's theme](/wiki/The_Force_Theme "The Force Theme")," the "[Jawa theme](/wiki/Jawa_Sandcrawler "Jawa Sandcrawler")," the "[Rebel Fanfare](/wiki/Rebel_Fanfare "Rebel Fanfare")," and the "[Imperial motif](/wiki/Imperial_motif "Imperial motif")"). He then went on to create the [actual score](/wiki/Musical_score "Musical score") by stringing all the themes he created together in a way that would match up with what was happening on screen.[[40]](#cite_note-Films_and_Filming_JW_interview-40) It was unknown exactly how long John Williams spent writing the score, but it is certain that he would have had at the absolute most no more than 8 weeks, given that they started recording on March 5th. This is unrealistic because there needed to have been time for the orchestrators to write out all the various parts for the players, so it is more likely that the score was completed in 7 weeks or less.

As with any creative process, parts of the score went through multiple revisions. One well-known example is the cue "Lost R2", which scores the famous "binary sunset" scene. This scene was originally scored with a very different sounding piece that contained "Luke's theme". When Lucas heard the cue, he asked if it could be rescored with "Ben's theme" because he felt it fit the scene better.[[35]](#cite_note-1977_liner_notes-35) It can be argued that this opened the door for "Ben's theme" to be recontextualized into what we think of today as the "Force theme". Another interesting example of the score changing was the cue "A Home Destroyed". When this cue was written, it was designed to score the end of Ben's house, Leia's torture, the discovery of the attacked sandcrawler, and Luke returning home to find his guardians dead and his home burned. While Williams was writing the score, the film was re-edited so that the board room scene would occur where the torture scene used to be. This caused the cue to be split in half. The first 14 bars were recorded by themselves with a newly written ending featuring the "Death Star theme" for the transition to the boardroom scene. Then a second cue was recorded, being made up of bars 31-71 (attacked sandcrawler and burned homestead scenes) and bars 17-30 (Leia torture scene), with some new transition material written to join them.[[41]](#cite_note-jwfan_comment_explaining_A_Home_Destroyed-41) This isn't the only time editing of the film would require changes to the score, but it is one of the only examples where a re-edit resulted in the score being changed before it was recorded. The rest of the edits were done too late, and the remaining score changes were left to be made artificially by Ken Wannberg.[[38]](#cite_note-Paul_Hirsch_book-38) After the writing of the score was completed, the orchestrations were performed by lead orchestrator Herbert Spencer, who was assisted by Arthur Morton, Angela Morley, Al Woodbury, Alexander Courage and Williams himself.[[40]](#cite_note-Films_and_Filming_JW_interview-40)

[[43]](#cite_note-Jason_LeBlanc_spreadsheet-43)[[44]](#cite_note-orchestrator_credits-44)

When it came time to record the score, Williams was given no choice but to record in London, presumably due to budget constraints and the fact that most of the film was shot in England.[[37]](#cite_note-The_Making_of_Star_Wars_book-37) He did have the choice of which orchestra he wanted to work with, and he ended up choosing the [London Symphony Orchestra](/wiki/London_Symphony_Orchestra "London Symphony Orchestra") (LSO) due to its primary conductor being his friend André Previn. This was historically significant, as it was the first time Williams ever got to work with an organized symphony orchestra for a film.[[35]](#cite_note-1977_liner_notes-35) Previous films of his usually recorded with freelance players. The score was recorded over the course of eight days between March 5th and March 16th of 1977 at Anvil Recording Studios in Denham, England.[[34]](#cite_note-1997_liner_notes-34)[[35]](#cite_note-1977_liner_notes-35) People present at the sessions included John Williams himself, who was conducting, George Lucas, recording engineer Eric Tomlinson, his assistant Alan Snelling, and music editor Ken Wannberg. The orchestra itself was made up of 26 violins, 10 violas, 10 cellos, 6 basses, 11 woodwinds, 8 horns, 4 trumpets, 3 trombones, 2 tubas, 2 harps, 3 percussion, 1 timpani, 1 piano, and 1 celeste.[[45]](#cite_note-Gerhardt_liner_notes-45) The score was recorded with approximately 23 microphones, placed at strategic positions around the orchestra. The mixing console, a Rupert Neve, had 24 inputs and 16 outputs. Recording engineer Eric Tomlinson used the console to create a live LCR (Left, Center, Right) mix while the orchestra was playing. The live mixes were recorded straight to two 35mm magnetic film recorders (with healthy Dolby A noise reduction applied). The live mix was also routed to tracks 1-3 of a Struder A80 16-track 2 inch recorder, with sections of the orchestra isolated on tracks 4-15 and a 50 hz pilot tone on track 16. The pilot tone could later be used for synchronization with the film during editing.[[46]](#cite_note-Chris_Malone_document-46)[[47]](#cite_note-Alan_Snelling_interview-47) After the recording was completed, the best takes were combined into performance edits by music editor Ken Wannberg. He created performance edits using one of the 35mm mag recordings, as well as with the 16 track tapes. (note: a performance edit is where sections of different takes are combined together to create the best possible recording of a given cue) The 16 track tapes were intended both for backup purposes, and to be sent off to be remixed by John Neal for the eventual soundtrack release on LP. The 35mm edits would of course be further edited by Wannberg into the final stems for use in the film.[[46]](#cite_note-Chris_Malone_document-46)[[35]](#cite_note-1977_liner_notes-35)[[48]](#cite_note-jwfan_comment_about_john_neal_auction-48)
