| 102:07-103:25 | 10m3-11m1 | Stand By | The Rebel X-Wings approach the Death Star | Five microedits: the first 5 seconds are slowed by 7%, the next 13 seconds are slowed by 2%, the 1 second from 103:07-103:08 is looped once, the 2.5 seconds from 103:08-103:11 is looped once, a quarter second is snipped at 103:22 |
| 103:22-106:45 | 11m2 Rev. | Approaching the Target | The Battle of Yavin begins |  |
| 110:33-115:00 | 12m1 | The Last Battle | The Battle of Yavin ends, Luke blows up the Death Star | Two microedits: half a second snipped at 110:46, quarter second silence added at 114:33 |
| 115:33-117:20 | 12m2 | End Titles (bars 1-51) | Award Ceremony |  |
| 117:20-117:51 | 12m2X | End Titles | End Credits Sequence |  |
| 117:51-121:07 | 12m2 | End Titles | End Credits Sequence |  |

Total length of music in movie: 80:37

#### Soundtrack releases

The score to *Star Wars* has had several releases over the years. While many of these releases have been straight reissues of previous releases, there are currently four releases with unique programs that were independently mastered from the original session tapes:[[49]](#cite_note-explanation_of_releases-49)

* [1977 OST (20th Century Fox Records)](/wiki/Star_Wars_Episode_IV:_A_New_Hope_Original_Soundtrack "Star Wars Episode IV: A New Hope Original Soundtrack")
* [1993 Anthology (Arista Records)](/wiki/Star_Wars_Trilogy:_The_Original_Soundtrack_Anthology "Star Wars Trilogy: The Original Soundtrack Anthology")
* [1997 Special Edition (RCA Victor)](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_IV_A_New_Hope_Special_Edition:_Original_Motion_Picture_Soundtrack "Star Wars: Episode IV A New Hope Special Edition: Original Motion Picture Soundtrack")
* [2016 Sony Classical Ultimate Vinyl Collection](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Ultimate_Vinyl_Collection "Star Wars: The Ultimate Vinyl Collection")
* [2016 Sony Classical Ultimate Soundtrack Edition](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Ultimate_Soundtrack_Edition "Star Wars: The Ultimate Soundtrack Edition")
* [2016 Sony Classical Ultimate Digital Collection](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Ultimate_Digital_Collection "Star Wars: The Ultimate Digital Collection")
* [2018 OST Remaster (Walt Disney Records)](/wiki/Star_Wars_Episode_IV:_A_New_Hope_Remastered_Soundtrack "Star Wars Episode IV: A New Hope Remastered Soundtrack")

### Sound

*A New Hope* was originally presented in monaural sound in many theaters, though the first-run [70mm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/70mm_film "wikipedia:70mm film") prints were some of the earliest wide-release examples of surround sound—something not seen in the commercial cinema since the [Cinerama](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cinerama "wikipedia:Cinerama") and [Cinemascope](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cinemascope "wikipedia:Cinemascope") experiments of the early 1950s.

### Sources and inspirations

The film drew inspiration from a number of sources. This was conscious and has been acknowledged by George Lucas in interviews. It is characteristic of much myth-building.

Lucas has stated that Akira Kurosawa's [1958](/wiki/1950s "1950s") film *The Hidden Fortress* (USA release [1962](/wiki/1960s "1960s")) was a strong influence. The resemblance between the two buffoon farmers in *The Hidden Fortress* and the two talkative droids in *A New Hope* is apparent. Indeed, when the droids find themselves alone on Tatooine, even the music and the style of "wipe" cuts are a clear homage to *Hidden Fortress*. When [Motti](/wiki/Conan_Antonio_Motti "Conan Antonio Motti") is criticizing [Darth Vader](/wiki/Anakin_Skywalker "Anakin Skywalker"), he is about to mention the Rebels' "hidden fortress" before Vader cuts him off in the middle of the last word.

The climactic scene in which the Death Star is assaulted was modeled after (including some of the same dialogue) the 1950s film *[The Dam Busters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Dam_Busters_(film) "wikipedia:The Dam Busters (film)")*, in which [RAF](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Air_Force "wikipedia:Royal Air Force") [Lancaster bombers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avro_Lancaster "wikipedia:Avro Lancaster") fly along heavily defended reservoirs and aim "[bouncing bombs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bouncing_bomb "wikipedia:Bouncing bomb")" at German man-made dams in a bid to cripple the heavy industry of the [Ruhr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruhr "wikipedia:Ruhr"). (*A New Hope* cinematographer [Gilbert Taylor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gilber_Taylor "wikipedia:Gilber Taylor") had previously worked on the special-effects sequences for that film.)

Lucas has made mention of the film *[633 Squadron](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/633_Squadron "wikipedia:633 Squadron")* directed by [Walter Grauman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walter_Grauman "wikipedia:Walter Grauman") when citing movies that inspired themes or elements in *A New Hope*. The "trench run" in *A New Hope* wherein Luke flies his X-wing through a "trench" on the Death Star and destroys the ship was inspired, at least in small part, by the finale of 633 Squadron, which involves several Royal Air Force planes flying at low level up a fjord against heavy, ground-based anti-aircraft fire, to attack a factory located at the base of a cliff at the canyon's end.

## Release and reception

*Star Wars* debuted on May 25, 1977 in 32 theaters, and proceeded to break house records, effectively becoming one of the first [blockbuster](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blockbuster_(entertainment) "wikipedia:Blockbuster (entertainment)") films.[[50]](#cite_note-50) It remains one of the most financially successful films of all time. Some of the cast and crew noted lines of people stretching around theaters as they drove by. Even technical crew members, such as model makers, were asked for autographs, and cast members became instant household names.[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5) The film's original total U.S. gross came to $307,263,857, and it earned $6,806,951 during its first weekend in wide release. Lucas claimed that he had spent most of the release day in a sound studio in Los Angeles. When he went out for lunch with his then-wife Marcia, they encountered a long queue of people along the sidewalks leading to Mann's Chinese Theater, waiting to see *Star Wars*.[[23]](#cite_note-Heritage-23) The film became the highest-grossing film of 1977 and the highest-grossing film of all time until *[E.T. The Extra-Terrestrial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/E.T._the_Extra-Terrestrial "wikipedia:E.T. the Extra-Terrestrial")* broke that record in 1982. (With subsequent re-releases, *Star Wars* reclaimed the title, but lost it again to [James Cameron's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Cameron "wikipedia:James Cameron") 1997 blockbuster *[Titanic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film) "wikipedia:Titanic (1997 film)")*.) The film earned $797,900,000 worldwide, making it the first film to reach the $300 million mark.[[51]](#cite_note-Mojo-51) Adjusted for inflation it is the second highest grossing movie of all time in the United States, behind *[Gone with the Wind](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gone_with_the_Wind_(film) "wikipedia:Gone with the Wind (film)")*.[[52]](#cite_note-52)

In 1989, the U.S. [National Film Registry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Film_Registry "wikipedia:National Film Registry") of the [Library of Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Library_of_Congress "wikipedia:Library of Congress") selected the film as a "culturally, historically, or aesthetically important" film.[[53]](#cite_note-53) In 2006, Lucas' original screenplay was selected by the [Writers Guild of America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Writers_Guild_of_America,_East "wikipedia:Writers Guild of America, East") as the 68th greatest of all time.[[54]](#cite_note-54) The [American Film Institute](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Film_Institute "wikipedia:American Film Institute") (or AFI) listed it 15th on a list of the top 100 films of the 20th century.[[55]](#cite_note-AFImovies-55) The American Film Institute has named *Star Wars* and specific elements of it to several of its "top 100 lists" of American cinema, compiled as a part of the Institute's 100th anniversary celebration. These include the 27th most thrilling American film of all time;[[56]](#cite_note-AFIthrills-56) the thirty-ninth most inspirational American film of all-time;[[57]](#cite_note-AFIcheers-57) Han Solo as the fourteenth greatest American film hero of all time and Obi-Wan Kenobi thirty-seventh on the same list.[[58]](#cite_note-AFIhandv-58) The often repeated line "May the Force be with you" was ranked as the eighth greatest quote in American film history.[[59]](#cite_note-AFIquote-59) [John Williams](/wiki/John_Williams "John Williams")' score was ranked as the greatest American film score of all time.[[60]](#cite_note-AFIscore-60)

*Star Wars* won multiple awards at the [1978 Academy Awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/50th_Academy_Awards "wikipedia:50th Academy Awards"), including [Best Art Direction-Set Decoration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Art_Direction "wikipedia:Academy Award for Best Art Direction"), which went to [John Barry](/wiki/John_Barry "John Barry"), [Norman Reynolds](/wiki/Norman_Reynolds "Norman Reynolds"), [Leslie Dilley](/wiki/Leslie_Dilley "Leslie Dilley"), and [Roger Christian](/wiki/Roger_Christian "Roger Christian"). [Best Costume Design](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Costume_Design "wikipedia:Academy Award for Best Costume Design") was awarded to [John Mollo](/wiki/John_Mollo "John Mollo"); [Best Film Editing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Film_Editing "wikipedia:Academy Award for Film Editing") went to Paul Hirsch, Marcia Lucas and Richard Chew; [John Stears](/wiki/John_Stears "John Stears"), [John Dykstra](/wiki/John_Dykstra "John Dykstra"), [Richard Edlund](/wiki/Richard_Edlund "Richard Edlund"), [Grant McCune](/wiki/Grant_McCune "Grant McCune"), and [Robert Blalack](/wiki/Robert_Blalack "Robert Blalack") all received awards for [Best Effects, Visual Effects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Visual_Effects "wikipedia:Academy Award for Visual Effects"). John Williams was awarded his third Oscar for [Best Music, Original Score](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Original_Music_Score "wikipedia:Academy Award for Original Music Score"); the [Best Sound](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Sound "wikipedia:Academy Award for Sound") went to [Don MacDougall](/wiki/Don_MacDougall "Don MacDougall"), [Ray West](/wiki/Ray_West_(sound_editor) "Ray West (sound editor)"), [Bob Minkler](/wiki/Bob_Minkler "Bob Minkler") and [Derek Ball](/wiki/Derek_Ball "Derek Ball"); and a [Special Achievement for sound effects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Honorary_Award "wikipedia:Academy Honorary Award") went to Ben Burtt. Additional nominations included [Alec Guinness](/wiki/Alec_Guinness "Alec Guinness") for [Best Actor in a Supporting Role](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actor "wikipedia:Academy Award for Best Supporting Actor"), George Lucas for [Best Screenplay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Writing_Original_Screenplay "wikipedia:Academy Award for Writing Original Screenplay") and [Best Director](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Directing "wikipedia:Academy Award for Directing"), and Gary Kurtz was nominated for his producing duties in [Best Picture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Picture "wikipedia:Academy Award for Best Picture").[[61]](#cite_note-Oscars-61) At the [Golden Globe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Globe_Awards "wikipedia:Golden Globe Awards") awards, the film was nominated for [Best Motion Picture – Drama](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Motion_Picture_%E2%80%93_Drama "wikipedia:Golden Globe Award for Best Motion Picture – Drama"), [Best Director](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Director "wikipedia:Golden Globe Award for Best Director"), [Best Supporting Actor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actor "wikipedia:Golden Globe Award for Best Supporting Actor") (Alec Guinness), and [Best Original Score](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Original_Score "wikipedia:Golden Globe Award for Best Original Score"); it only won the award for Best Original Score.[[62]](#cite_note-Golden_Globe-62) It received six [BAFTA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Academy_of_Film_and_Television_Arts "wikipedia:British Academy of Film and Television Arts") nominations: [Best Film](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Film "wikipedia:BAFTA Award for Best Film"), [Best Editing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Editing "wikipedia:BAFTA Award for Best Editing"), [Best Costume Design](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Costume_Design "wikipedia:BAFTA Award for Best Costume Design"), [Best Production Design](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Production_Design "wikipedia:BAFTA Award for Best Production Design"), [Best Sound](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Sound "wikipedia:BAFTA Award for Best Sound"), and [Best Original Music](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Original_Music "wikipedia:BAFTA Award for Best Original Music"); the film won in the latter two categories.[[63]](#cite_note-BAFTA-63) John Williams won three [Grammy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grammy_Awards "wikipedia:Grammy Awards") awards for [Best Original Score Written for a Motion Picture or a Television Special](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Score_Soundtrack_for_Visual_Media "wikipedia:Grammy Award for Best Score Soundtrack for Visual Media"), [Best Pop Instrumental Performance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Pop_Instrumental_Performance "wikipedia:Grammy Award for Best Pop Instrumental Performance"), and [Best Instrumental Composition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Instrumental_Composition "wikipedia:Grammy Award for Best Instrumental Composition").[[64]](#cite_note-Grammys-64) The film was awarded the [Hugo Award](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hugo_Award "wikipedia:Hugo Award") for Best Dramatic Presentation.[[65]](#cite_note-Hugo_Awards-65) In 1997, the [MTV Movie Awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MTV_Movie_Awards "wikipedia:MTV Movie Awards") awarded Chewbacca the lifetime achievement award for his work in the *Star Wars* trilogy.[[66]](#cite_note-MTV_1997-66)

Originally, if the film did poorly at the box office, Lucas planned to turn the novel *[Splinter of the Mind's Eye](/wiki/Splinter_of_the_Mind%27s_Eye "Splinter of the Mind's Eye")* into a low-budget sequel to the movie. According to an interview with Alan Dean Foster in *[Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empire_(magazine) "wikipedia:Empire (magazine)")* magazine, the book was written to be filmed as a low-budget sequel if *Star Wars* was not a huge success. Harrison Ford was not signed for the sequel as of the writing of the book, which is why Han Solo does not appear in the novel. However, with the success of *A New Hope*, Lucas was free to make *The Empire Strikes Back*.[[67]](#cite_note-Year_by_Year_new-67)

Wary that *Star Wars* would be beaten out by other summer films, such as *[Smokey and the Bandit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smokey_and_the_Bandit "wikipedia:Smokey and the Bandit")*, 20th Century Fox moved the release date to Wednesday before [Memorial Day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Memorial_Day "wikipedia:Memorial Day"): [May 25](/wiki/May_25 "May 25"), [1977](/wiki/1977 "1977"). However, few theaters ordered the film to be shown. In response, 20th Century Fox demanded that theaters order *Star Wars* if they wanted an eagerly anticipated film based on a best-selling novel titled *[The Other Side of Midnight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Other_Side_of_Midnight "wikipedia:The Other Side of Midnight")*.[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5) *[The New York Times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_New_York_Times "wikipedia:The New York Times")* published the first advertisements for the film on [May 15](/wiki/May_15 "May 15"), only ten days before its premiere.[[68]](#cite_note-Season_2_Directors-68)

*Star Wars* became an instant success upon release; within three weeks, 20th Century Fox's stock price doubled to a record high. Before 1977, 20th Century Fox's greatest annual profits were $37,000,000; in 1977, the company earned $79,000,000. Although the film's cultural neutrality helped it to gain international success, Ladd became anxious during the premiere in [Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japan "wikipedia:Japan"). After the screening, the audience was silent, leading Ladd, Jr. to fear that the film would be unsuccessful. He was later told that, in Japan, silence was the greatest honor to a film. Meanwhile, thousands attended a ceremony at [Grauman's Chinese Theater](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grauman%27s_Chinese_Theater "wikipedia:Grauman's Chinese Theater"), where C-3PO, R2-D2 and Darth Vader placed their footprints in the theater's forecourt.[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5)

During the film's original theatrical run, there were a number of television promotions:

* Darth Vader on *[The Wacko Saturday Morning Preview and Other Good Stuff Special](https://lostmediawiki.com/The_Wacko_Saturday_Morning_Preview_and_Other_Good_Stuff_Special_(lost_CBS_preview_special;_1977))* (September 8, 1977)
* Darth Vader on The ABC All-Star Saturday preview show (September 9, 1977)[[69]](#cite_note-All-Star-69)
* A re-creation of the cantina set for *[The Richard Pryor Show](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Richard_Pryor_Show "wikipedia:The Richard Pryor Show")* (September 13, 1977)
* *[The Making of Star Wars](/wiki/The_Making_of_Star_Wars "The Making of Star Wars")* TV special (September 16, 1977)
* A *Star Wars*–themed *[Donnie and Marie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donny_%26_Marie_(1976_TV_series) "wikipedia:Donny & Marie (1976 TV series)")* episode (September 23, 1977)
* Mark Hamill on *[The Bob Hope All Star Christmas Comedy Special](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Hope_television_specials "wikipedia:Bob Hope television specials")* (December 19, 1977)
* [Bill Murray](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Murray "wikipedia:Bill Murray")'s "[Nick The Lounge Singer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recurring_Saturday_Night_Live_characters_and_sketches_introduced_1976%E2%80%931977#Nick_The_Lounge_Singer "wikipedia:Recurring Saturday Night Live characters and sketches introduced 1976–1977")" singing the *Star Wars* Main Theme on *[Saturday Night Live](/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live "Saturday Night Live")* (January 28, 1978)
* *[The Star Wars Holiday Special](/wiki/The_Star_Wars_Holiday_Special "The Star Wars Holiday Special")* (November 17, 1978)[[70]](#cite_note-tvparty-70)
* Carrie Fisher on *Saturday Night Live* (November 18, 1978)
* *[American Graffitti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Graffiti "wikipedia:American Graffiti")*'s [Wolfman Jack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wolfman_Jack "wikipedia:Wolfman Jack") interviews Darth Vader on *[The Midnight Special](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Midnight_Special_(TV_show) "wikipedia:The Midnight Special (TV show)")*. (unknown date)[[71]](#cite_note-Wolfman-71)

## Adaptations and tie-in media

[Charles Lippincott](/wiki/Charles_Lippincott "Charles Lippincott") was hired by Lucas' production company, [Lucasfilm](/wiki/Lucasfilm "Lucasfilm"), as marketing director for *Star Wars*. Because 20th Century Fox gave little support for marketing beyond licensing T-shirts and posters, Lippincott was forced to look elsewhere. He secured deals with [Stan Lee](/wiki/Stan_Lee "Stan Lee"), [Roy Thomas](/wiki/Roy_Thomas "Roy Thomas") and [Marvel Comics](/wiki/Marvel_Comics "Marvel Comics") for a comic book adaptation and with [Del Rey](/wiki/Del_Rey "Del Rey") Books for a novelization. Although *Star Wars* merchandise was available to enthusiastic children upon release, only [Kenner Toys](/wiki/Kenner_Products "Kenner Products")—who believed that the film would be unsuccessful—had accepted Lippincott's licensing offers. Kenner responded to the sudden demand for toys by selling boxed vouchers in its "empty box" Christmas campaign; these vouchers could be redeemed for [the toys](/wiki/Star_Wars_(Kenner_toy_line) "Star Wars (Kenner toy line)") in March 1978.[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5)

The [novelization](/wiki/Star_Wars:_A_New_Hope_(novelization) "Star Wars: A New Hope (novelization)") of the film was published in December 1976, six months before the film was released. The credited author was George Lucas, but the book was revealed to have been [ghostwritten](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghostwriter "wikipedia:Ghostwriter") by [Alan Dean Foster](/wiki/Alan_Dean_Foster "Alan Dean Foster"), who later wrote the first [Expanded Universe](/wiki/Star_Wars_Legends "Star Wars Legends") novel, *[Splinter of the Mind's Eye](/wiki/Splinter_of_the_Mind%27s_Eye "Splinter of the Mind's Eye")*. The book was first published as *Star Wars: From the Adventures of Luke Skywalker*; later editions were titled simply *Star Wars* and, later, *Star Wars Episode IV: A New Hope*, to reflect the retitling of the film. Certain scenes deleted from the film (and later restored or archived in DVD bonus features) were present in the novel, such as Luke at Tosche Station with Biggs and the encounter between Han and Jabba in [Docking Bay 94](/wiki/Docking_Bay_94 "Docking Bay 94"). Other deleted scenes from the movie, such as a close-up of a stormtrooper riding on a [Dewback](/wiki/Dewback "Dewback"), were included in a photo insert added to later printings of the book. Smaller details were also changed; for example, in the Death Star assault, Luke's callsign is Blue Five instead of Red Five as in the film. Lippincott secured the deal with Del Rey Books to publish the novelization in November 1976. By February 1977, a half million copies had been sold.[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5)

A [radio drama](/wiki/Star_Wars_(radio) "Star Wars (radio)") adaptation of the film was written by [Brian Daley](/wiki/Brian_Daley "Brian Daley"), directed by [John Madden](/wiki/John_Madden "John Madden"), and produced for and broadcast on the American [National Public Radio](/wiki/National_Public_Radio "National Public Radio") network in 1981. The adaptation received cooperation from [George Lucas](/wiki/George_Lucas "George Lucas"), who donated the rights to NPR. John Williams' music and Ben Burtt's sound design were retained for the show; Mark Hamill (Luke Skywalker) and Anthony Daniels (C-3PO) reprised their roles as well. The radio drama featured scenes not seen in the final cut of the film, such as Luke Skywalker's observation of the space battle above Tatooine through binoculars, a skyhopper race, and Darth Vader's interrogation of Princess Leia. In terms of [*Star Wars* canon](/wiki/Canon "Canon"), the radio drama is given the highest designation, G-canon.[[72]](#cite_note-Blog-holocron|4-72)

Over the years, several comic adaptations of the film have been produced:

* [Marvel Comics](/wiki/Star_Wars_(1977) "Star Wars (1977)") launched their Star Wars series with a six-part adaptation of the film written by [Roy Thomas](/wiki/Roy_Thomas "Roy Thomas") and illustrated by [Howard Chaykin](/wiki/Howard_Chaykin "Howard Chaykin").
* In 1978, [Al Williamson](/wiki/Al_Williamson "Al Williamson") worked on an adaptation in comic strip form that was never released.
* Concurrently with the release of the 1997 Special Edition, [Dark Horse Comics](/wiki/Dark_Horse_Comics "Dark Horse Comics") released a new [four-part adaptation](/wiki/Star_Wars:_A_New_Hope_-_The_Special_Edition "Star Wars: A New Hope - The Special Edition") written by [Bruce Jones](/wiki/Bruce_Jones "Bruce Jones") and illustrated by [Eduardo Barreto](/wiki/Eduardo_Barreto "Eduardo Barreto").
* A [manga adaptation](/wiki/Star_Wars_Manga:_A_New_Hope "Star Wars Manga: A New Hope") illustrated by [Hisao Tamaki](/wiki/Hisao_Tamaki "Hisao Tamaki") was released in Japan in 1997 and in the United States in 1998.

### Re-releases

The film was originally released as—and consequently often called—*Star Wars*, without *Episode IV* or the subtitle *A New Hope*. The 1980 sequel, [*Star Wars*: Episode V *The Empire Strikes Back*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_V_The_Empire_Strikes_Back "Star Wars: Episode V The Empire Strikes Back"), featured the episode number and subtitle in the opening crawl. When the original film was re-released on [April 10](/wiki/April_10 "April 10"), 1981, *Episode IV: A New Hope* was added above the original opening crawl.[[73]](#cite_note-Shakespeare_meets_TROS-73) Although Lucas claims that only six films were ever planned, representatives of Lucasfilm discussed plans for nine or 12 possible films in early interviews.[[74]](#cite_note-74) The film was re-released theatrically in 1978, 1979, 1981, 1982, and 1997.

 [![Official poster for A New Hope  release](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/9d/Star_Wars_1997_re-release_poster.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20250617061207) [![Official poster for A New Hope  release](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/9d/Star_Wars_1997_re-release_poster.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/180?cb=20250617061207)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/9d/Star_Wars_1997_re-release_poster.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20250617061207) 

Official poster for *A New Hope* [Special Edition](/wiki/The_Star_Wars_Trilogy_Special_Edition "The Star Wars Trilogy Special Edition") release

 

After ILM used [computer generated effects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_generated_imagery "wikipedia:Computer generated imagery") for Steven Spielberg's *[Jurassic Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jurassic_Park_(film) "wikipedia:Jurassic Park (film)")*, Lucas concluded that digital technology had caught up to his original vision for *Star Wars*.[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5) As part of *Star Wars*' 20th anniversary celebration in 1997, *A New Hope* was digitally remastered and re-released to theaters, along with *The Empire Strikes Back* and *[Return of the Jedi](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_VI_Return_of_the_Jedi "Star Wars: Episode VI Return of the Jedi")*, under the campaign title *[The Star Wars Trilogy: Special Edition](/wiki/The_Star_Wars_Trilogy_Special_Edition "The Star Wars Trilogy Special Edition")*. The Special Edition versions contained visual shots and scenes that were unachievable in the original release due to financial, technological, and time restraints; one such scene involved a meeting between Han Solo and [Jabba the Hutt](/wiki/Jabba_Desilijic_Tiure "Jabba Desilijic Tiure").[[5]](#cite_note-EmpireOfDreams-5) Although most changes were minor or cosmetic in nature, some fans believe that Lucas degraded the movie with the additions.[[75]](#cite_note-Changes-75) For instance, a controversial change in which Greedo shoots first when confronting Han Solo has inspired T-shirts brandishing the phrase "[Han shot first](/wiki/Han_shot_first "Han shot first")."[[76]](#cite_note-HSF-76)

### Home video

:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [Star Wars home video releases](/wiki/Star_Wars_home_video_releases "Star Wars home video releases")
:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [Star Wars Trilogy (DVD)](/wiki/Star_Wars_Trilogy_(DVD) "Star Wars Trilogy (DVD)")

*A New Hope* was released on [DVD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DVD "wikipedia:DVD") on [September 21](/wiki/September_21 "September 21"), [2004](/wiki/2004 "2004") in a box set with *The Empire Strikes Back*, *Return of the Jedi*, and a bonus disc of supplemental material. The movies were digitally restored and remastered, and [more changes were made](/wiki/List_of_changes_in_Star_Wars_re-releases#A_New_Hope_3 "List of changes in Star Wars re-releases") by George Lucas.

The DVD features a commentary track from George Lucas, Ben Burtt, Dennis Muren, and Carrie Fisher. The bonus disc contains the documentary *[Empire of Dreams: The Story of the Star Wars Trilogy](/wiki/Empire_of_Dreams:_The_Story_of_the_Star_Wars_Trilogy "Empire of Dreams: The Story of the Star Wars Trilogy")*, three featurettes, teaser and theatrical trailers, TV spots, still galleries, an exclusive preview of *Star Wars*: Episode III *Revenge of the Sith*, a playable [Xbox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xbox "wikipedia:Xbox") demo of the [LucasArts](/wiki/LucasArts "LucasArts") game *[Star Wars: Battlefront](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Battlefront "Star Wars: Battlefront")*, and a "Making Of" documentary on the [*Episode III* video game](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_III_Revenge_of_the_Sith_(video_game) "Star Wars: Episode III Revenge of the Sith (video game)"). The set was reissued in December 2005 as part of a three-disc "limited edition" boxed set without the bonus disc.

:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [Original unaltered trilogy](/wiki/Original_unaltered_trilogy "Original unaltered trilogy")

The trilogy was re-released on separate two-disc Limited Edition DVD sets from [September 12](/wiki/September_12 "September 12"), 2006 to [December 31](/wiki/December_31 "December 31"), [2006](/wiki/2006 "2006"); the original versions of the films were added as bonus material. Controversy surrounded the release (often referred to as "George's [original unaltered trilogy](/wiki/Original_unaltered_trilogy "Original unaltered trilogy")," or "GOUT" for short) because the so-called "unaltered" versions were from the 1993 non-[anamorphic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anamorphic "wikipedia:Anamorphic") [laserdisc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laserdisc "wikipedia:Laserdisc") masters, and were not re-transferred to modern DVD standards.[[77]](#cite_note-77)

It was re-released in the Blu-ray format on [September 16](/wiki/September_16 "September 16"), [2011](/wiki/2011 "2011").[[78]](#cite_note-SWArchive-Bring_the_Complete_Collection_Home:_''Star_Wars:_The_Complete_Saga''_on_Blu-Ray-78)

On [April 7](/wiki/April_7 "April 7"), [2015](/wiki/2015 "2015"), the Walt Disney Studios, 20th Century Fox, and Lucasfilm jointly announced the digital releases of the six released *Star Wars* films. Fox released *A New Hope* for digital download on April 10, 2015 (while Disney released the other five films).[[79]](#cite_note-SW-The_''Star_Wars''_Digital_Movie_Collection_Coming_April_10-79)

Despite The Walt Disney Company's [2012](/wiki/2012 "2012") purchase of Lucasfilm and the release rights to all future *Star Wars* films, Fox was to retain original distribution rights to *A New Hope*, which they co-produced and co-financed, in perpetuity in all media worldwide. Fox was also to retain theatrical, nontheatrical, and home video rights worldwide for the franchise's five subsequent films, which Lucasfilm produced and financed independently, through [May](/wiki/May "May") [2020](/wiki/2020 "2020"), at which time ownership was to transfer to Disney. This complex relationship between Fox and Disney, particularly in regards to Fox's perpetual rights to Episode IV, was to create an obstacle for any future boxed set comprising all nine films.[[80]](#cite_note-Hollywood_Reporter-80) On [December 14](/wiki/December_14 "December 14"), [2017](/wiki/2017 "2017"), The Walt Disney Company announced that it was acquiring most of Fox's parent company, [21st Century Fox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/21st_Century_Fox "wikipedia:21st Century Fox"), including the film studio and all distribution rights to *A New Hope*.[[81]](#cite_note-Acquire-81) On [March 20](/wiki/March_20 "March 20"), 2019, the [deal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acquisition_of_21st_Century_Fox_by_Disney "wikipedia:Acquisition of 21st Century Fox by Disney") was officially completed.[[82]](#cite_note-82) On [April 12](/wiki/April_12 "April 12"), 2019, a [Blu-ray](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blu-ray "wikipedia:Blu-ray") box set containing the nine main installments of the *[Star Wars](/wiki/Star_Wars "Star Wars")* [saga](/wiki/Star_Wars_saga "Star Wars saga") remastered in 4K was reportedly announced to be in development for a 2020 release.[[83]](#cite_note-83)

## Deleted scenes ‡

There are many short alternate takes throughout *Star Wars* where Luke appears in his poncho: Luke in the desert, in the Tusken Raiders' canyon, Luke finding the destroyed homestead, and in the hangar on [Yavin 4](/wiki/Yavin_4 "Yavin 4"). The only poncho scenes that made the final cut were in [Docking Bay 94](/wiki/Docking_Bay_94 "Docking Bay 94"), on the *Millennium Falcon* flight from the Death Star, and on arrival on Yavin 4.

### Aunt Beru's Blue Milk

[Beru](/wiki/Beru_Whitesun_Lars "Beru Whitesun Lars") is in the homestead, pouring a [blue liquid](/wiki/Blue_milk "Blue milk") into a jug.

### Luke in the Desert

 [![Luke with his ](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/ad/EP4_luke_watching_battle.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20080318123235) [![Luke with his ](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/ad/EP4_luke_watching_battle.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/180?cb=20080318123235)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/ad/EP4_luke_watching_battle.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20080318123235) 

Luke with his [macrobinoculars](/wiki/Macrobinoculars "Macrobinoculars")

 

[Luke Skywalker](/wiki/Luke_Skywalker "Luke Skywalker") is in the Tatooine desert repairing a [moisture vaporator](/wiki/Moisture_vaporator "Moisture vaporator"), assisted by a [Treadwell](/wiki/WED_Treadwell_repair_droid "WED Treadwell repair droid") droid, when he notices shining objects in the sky. With his macrobinoculars Luke sees two ships engaged in combat beyond the atmosphere. He jumps into his [landspeeder](/wiki/Landspeeder "Landspeeder"). The malfunctioning Treadwell blows a fuse and is unable to follow. Luke speeds off into the desert to find his friends. The scene originally occurred after the *[Tantive IV](/wiki/Tantive_IV "Tantive IV")* is boarded, just before Darth Vader's first appearance in the film. It is thought that there is no longer any clear footage of this scene available. Existing footage has been degraded by poor film storage conditions over the years. Before the film was cut, this was the audience's first sight of the young Luke Skywalker, much earlier than in the final cut. It was removed along with subsequent scenes of Luke and his friends in [Anchorhead](/wiki/Anchorhead "Anchorhead"). George Lucas had originally written the scenes and shot them at the suggestion of his industry friends who thought that audiences wouldn't understand the story strictly being told from a droid's point of view. Upon realizing that the story was really about the droids' adventures and it was them leading things to Luke and Obi-Wan, etc. Lucas took the footage out.

### Tosche Station

Luke's landspeeder races into the town of Anchorhead, nearly running over an old woman. Luke rushes into [Tosche Station](/wiki/Tosche_Station "Tosche Station") excitedly telling his friends about the battle above their planet. He is overjoyed to be reunited with his friend [Biggs Darklighter](/wiki/Biggs_Darklighter "Biggs Darklighter") who is on planet leave from the Academy. [Deak](/wiki/Deacon "Deacon"), [Windy](/wiki/Windy_Starkiller "Windy Starkiller"), [Camie](/wiki/Camie_Loneozner "Camie Loneozner"), [Fixer](/wiki/Laze_Loneozner "Laze Loneozner") and Biggs all follow Luke outside to see the battle with Luke's macrobinoculars. The battle appears to have ended and Luke's friends ridicule him for making it all up. This scene was to come just after R2-D2 and C-3PO eject from the *Tantive IV* in an escape pod, and before the scene where [Princess](/wiki/Princess "Princess") [Leia](/wiki/Leia_Skywalker_Organa_Solo "Leia Skywalker Organa Solo") is led captive before Darth Vader. This scene establishes Luke's difficult relationships with his peers, and gives a picture of life on Tatooine. Storyline pacing may have been the deciding factor, but it should also be borne in mind that after Lucas's first screening of the rough cut of *Star Wars* in 1977, a fellow filmmaker jokingly accused him of producing "*American Graffiti* in space." This jibe probably influenced Lucas to cut the scenes set in Anchorhead. The sequence where Luke nearly runs down an old woman was an effects shot that was never completed.

### Luke and Biggs

 [![Luke says farewell to Biggs](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/f/f0/LukeBiggs2-MOSW.png/revision/latest?cb=20131104045913) [![Luke says farewell to Biggs](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/f/f0/LukeBiggs2-MOSW.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/180?cb=20131104045913)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/f/f0/LukeBiggs2-MOSW.png/revision/latest?cb=20131104045913) 

Luke says farewell to Biggs

 

This scene is a conversation between Luke and his oldest friend, Biggs Darklighter. Biggs has left Tatooine and is on planet leave from the [Imperial Academy](/wiki/Imperial_Academy "Imperial Academy") where he is training to be a space pilot. Luke's envy of Biggs's success conflicts with his duty to his uncle and his reasons for remaining on Tatooine. Biggs quietly tells Luke that he has decided to join the Rebellion against the Empire. In a tense and emotional conversation, the two young men say their final farewells. This scene was to come in between the scene where C-3PO spots a distant Jawa sandcrawler in the desert, and the capture of R2-D2 by the Jawas in the canyon. The Luke and Biggs sequence was part of the whole Anchorhead backstory on Tatooine, and was cut along with the other early scenes on Tatooine, probably for reasons of story pacing.

### Vader and Chief Bast

In this short scene, Darth Vader and Chief [Bast](/wiki/Moradmin_Bast "Moradmin Bast") walk along a corridor on the Death Star. Bast reports that the search for the missing droids has extended to Mos Eisley spaceport. Vader observes that Princess Leia is resisting interrogation, and Bast boldly criticizes [Tarkin](/wiki/Wilhuff_Tarkin "Wilhuff Tarkin")'s plan to break her as "foolish." The scene would have appeared between the scene where Han Solo encounters Jabba the Hutt in [Docking Bay 94](/wiki/Docking_Bay_94 "Docking Bay 94") (also cut), and the scene where Luke and Ben find the *[Millennium Falcon](/wiki/Millennium_Falcon "Millennium Falcon")* in Docking Bay 94.

### The Search for R2

 [![C-3PO pilots the landspeeder](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/SearchForArtoo-MOSW.png/revision/latest?cb=20131104055201) [![C-3PO pilots the landspeeder](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/SearchForArtoo-MOSW.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/180?cb=20131104055201)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/SearchForArtoo-MOSW.png/revision/latest?cb=20131104055201) 

C-3PO pilots the landspeeder

 

R2-D2 has absconded from his new master, Luke Skywalker. Early in the morning, Luke and Threepio rush off in the landspeeder to search for R2, with Threepio driving the landspeeder. They talk about Artoo, Ben Kenobi, and how angry Uncle Owen is going to be. The scene belongs at the start of the sequence where Luke and 3PO search for R2, before the attack of the [Tusken Raiders](/wiki/Tusken_Raider "Tusken Raider"). The moment was scored with a light version of Luke's theme; the music can be heard at the beginning of the cue "Land of the Sand People" on the original LP and CD configurations, or "Landspeeder Search" in the Special Edition album. Before the days of CGI, scenes like this landspeeder cockpit sequence had to be filmed against a rear-projection screen. The scene was dropped due to poor quality.

### Stormtrooper Search

Various alien creatures are seen walking around a narrow street in Mos Eisley, and some Stormtroopers walk past.

### Darth Vader widens the Search

This is a scene with Darth Vader and another Imperial officer on the [Death Star](/wiki/Death_Star "Death Star").

[↑](#cite_ref-explanation_of_releases_49-0) By comparing the credits for all releases from 1977 to present (7/1/22), we can conclude that the only teams that went back to the original masters were the OST (1977 - led by John Williams), Anthology (1993 - led by Ford A Thaxton), SE (1997 - led by Michael Mattessino), UEs (2016), and Remastered (2018 - led by Shawn Murphy). Every other release is a reissue of one of these seven 50.
